    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer8320973881949300128">In <i>Wishful Drinking</i>, Carrie Fisher tells the true and intoxicating story of her life with inimitable wit. Born to celebrity parents, she was picked to play a princess in a little movie called <i>Star Wars</i> when only 19 years old. "But it isn't all sweetness and light sabres." Alas, aside from a demanding career and her role as a single mother (not to mention the hyperspace hai</span>
  <span id="freeText8320973881949300128" style="display:none">In <i>Wishful Drinking</i>, Carrie Fisher tells the true and intoxicating story of her life with inimitable wit. Born to celebrity parents, she was picked to play a princess in a little movie called <i>Star Wars</i> when only 19 years old. "But it isn't all sweetness and light sabres." Alas, aside from a demanding career and her role as a single mother (not to mention the hyperspace hairdo), Carrie also spends her free time battling addiction, weathering the wild ride of manic depression and lounging around various mental institutions. It's an incredible tale—from having Elizabeth Taylor as a stepmother, to marrying (and divorcing) Paul Simon, from having the father of her daughter leave her for a man, to ultimately waking up one morning and finding a friend dead beside her in bed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8320973881949300128" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_78529577" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78529577" />
    <a title="Buck" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1450485-buck"><img alt="Buck" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1345474554p2/1450485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78529577?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buck" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buck" href="/user/show/1450485-buck">Buck</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439153710" href="/book/show/6734757-wishful-drinking">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1450485-buck?shelf=life-writing">life-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1450485-buck?shelf=chicks-dig-it">chicks-dig-it</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78529577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer764786483182426775">When the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy came out, I was too young to have nurtured any grotty, pubescent fantasies about Princess Leia (though I guess by the time of <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, I was old enough to be confusedly excited by those harem scenes with Jabba the Hutt). But now that I’ve read <i>Wishful Drinking</i>, I kind of want Carrie Fisher for my girlfriend. Except that she’s my mother’s age. And she’s a recovering alcoholic/drug addict with bipolar disorder and a lavishly messed-up family. Other th</span>
  <span id="freeText764786483182426775" style="display:none">When the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy came out, I was too young to have nurtured any grotty, pubescent fantasies about Princess Leia (though I guess by the time of <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, I was old enough to be confusedly excited by those harem scenes with Jabba the Hutt). But now that I’ve read <i>Wishful Drinking</i>, I kind of want Carrie Fisher for my girlfriend. Except that she’s my mother’s age. And she’s a recovering alcoholic/drug addict with bipolar disorder and a lavishly messed-up family. Other than that, though, she’s really great: she’s smart as a whip, wickedly funny and she swears like a teamster, whatever that is.<br /><br />All the same, I definitely wouldn’t want her for a daughter, or even a distant cousin. When it comes to her family’s dirty laundry—of which there are piles and piles lying around, hopelessly soiled—she’s not what you’d call the soul of discretion:<br /><br /><i>My father is beyond likeable. I mean you would just love him. My father also smokes four joints a day. Not for medical reasons. So I call him Puff Daddy. But he is just adorable. There’s a reason he got all that high-quality pussy—except for the Miss Louisiana thing, and anyone can make one mistake.</i><br /><br />How often do you find the word ‘father’ and the phrase ‘high-quality pussy’ in the same paragraph? Right, not very. And it takes a special kind of daughter to describe her mother’s sexual orientation in the following terms: ‘Not that it matters, but <i>my mother is not a lesbian</i>. She’s just a really, really bad heterosexual.’<br /><br />I’m not exactly up on Hollywood tell-alls, so maybe I’m overlooking some classics of the genre, but I don’t imagine there’d be that many celebrities out there who are blessed with either Fisher’s command of the American vernacular or her healthy perspective on her own fame:<br /><br /><i>Speaking of graves, I tell my younger friends that one day they’ll be at a bar playing pool and they’ll look up at the television set and there will be a picture of Princess Leia with two dates underneath, and they’ll say “awww—she said that would happen.” And they’ll go back to playing pool.</i><br /><br />Or there's this:<br /><br /><i>You know what’s funny about death? I mean other than absolutely nothing at all? You’d think we could remember finding out we weren’t immortal. Sometimes I see children sobbing in airports and I think, “Aww. They’ve just been told.”</i><br /><br />See, that’s clever, but isn't it also just the teensiest bit profound? Okay, not Schopenhauer profound, but still.<br /><br /><i>Wishful Drinking</i> is fluff, I guess, in the sense that it won’t change your life or even your lunch break. But it’s good, witty fluff. True, Fisher’s relentless wisecracking starts to sound needy and defensive after a while—he said, casually lobbing a rock from his glass house—but I think it’s to her credit that, despite her freakish Hollywood existence, she’s still human enough to laugh at herself. Come to think of it, what could be more freakish than that: a human being in Hollywood? It must get awfully lonely for her. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="764786483182426775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7371586019048663061" style="display:none">Audiobook - Library Overdrive- I downloaded this on a whim - it was available. I think this is the shortest Audiobook I’ve ever listened to - yet many topics are covered. <br /><br />There was a lot I didn’t know - including that Carrie Fisher was married - not long - to Paul Simon. <br />Actually there was a lot I didn’t know — I didn’t follow any news about Princess Leia from Star Wars. I knew nothing about her childhood - her absent father - her history with drugs - her history with a variety of psychiatrists and different therapies including shock therapy - <br /><br />Her memoir — which was adapted from one of her stage shows- gives us a panoramic view of what Carrie Fisher’s life was like : EXTREME HIGHS and EXTREME LOWS....NOT LIKE MOST CHILDREN’S growing years —-with Debbie Reynolds as her mother and growing up with ‘stars’ as family friends. So sad for the lost of both Carrie and Debbie Reynolds. <br /><br />I laughed at how much I understood from Carries point of view - that when she watched “The Father’s Knows Best” show.....she thought THAT was what ALL NORMAL families were like ( since she soon figured out her life wasn’t normal) .... Ha!....As if the “The Father’s Knows Best” TV Show represented reality. I wished it did. <br /><br />This quote of Carries speaks volumes: <br /> “If my life wasn’t funny it would just be true, and that would be unacceptable”. <br /><br />Great audiobook! Beautiful tribute to Carry Fisher. I fell in love with her myself. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1871721714" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1871721714" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1871721714?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1871721714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13916310638803107611">Turning to the first of her short memoirs, I was faced with some of Carrie Fisher's most interesting sentiments and humorous anecdotes detailing a life about which I knew very little. Fisher adds as an opening disclaimer that she underwent electro-convulsive therapy (ECT), which erased some of her past memories, so things within these pages might not be as clear or succinct as their actual occurrences. Born in the worst possible situation, the offspring of two Hollywood stars, Carrie Fisher foun</span>
  <span id="freeText13916310638803107611" style="display:none">Turning to the first of her short memoirs, I was faced with some of Carrie Fisher's most interesting sentiments and humorous anecdotes detailing a life about which I knew very little. Fisher adds as an opening disclaimer that she underwent electro-convulsive therapy (ECT), which erased some of her past memories, so things within these pages might not be as clear or succinct as their actual occurrences. Born in the worst possible situation, the offspring of two Hollywood stars, Carrie Fisher found herself in the middle of the most complex family tree imaginable. With Eddie Fisher (an apparently famous crooner of the 1950s) and Debbie Reynolds (famous Hollywood starlet at a young age) as parents, Fisher was forced to live in their blinding glory and make a name for herself. However, as with many star-studded couples, her parents moved on to bigger and better things, leaving her as a child of divorce. Does she use this excuse to explain away her decision to turn to drugs and alcohol? Not at all, or at least no more than any other child. Fisher tells of a life both in Los Angeles and New York, following her mother along her successful but fading career before she ended up on the set of Star Wars at nineteen and carving out a name for herself. This single character (Princess Leia) has permeated Fisher's very being and she was forever unable to shake its presence. Pulling out some stories about her interactions with George Lucas to explain why wearing a bra on set would not make scientific sense, her brief marriage to Paul Simon, and eventually marrying a man who got her pregnant and eventually announced that he was gay, Fisher takes the reader through a whirlwind tour of some of her most memorable moments, all surrounding an ever-increasing dependence on pills, psychiatrists, and flashes of fame. An interesting smattering of thoughts and memories, instilled with enough humour to leave the reader feeling this is an extended comedy dialogue, Fisher presents something to tide the reader over between larger and more substantial reading assignments. Funny for what it is, but not a stellar piece for those seeking an in-depth exploration of Carrie Fisher's life.<br /><br />Some might wonder why I am reading Carrie Fisher after I panned her two novels so recently. I knew what I was getting into with this book and it delivered precisely what I expected. While I might have preferred something more linear, I found myself interested in all the adventures, follies, and downright stupidity that crossed Fisher's path. I knew her only as Princess Leia (though I was not one to plaster posters upon my wall) and so all of this proved both intriguing and even a little entertaining. Fisher does not try to gussy up her writing or her stories. They are precisely as she remembers them, though she does remind the reader of her ECT throughout the piece, which acts as a means to understand some of the more random commentaries found herein. Engaging and even a little provocative, Fisher serves her purpose by presenting this piece, the first in what became a series. We shall see what else comes to pass as the Force flows through me for the other two memoir-ish publications.<br /><br />Kudos, Madam Fisher for entertaining and intriguing me. A nice appetizer before I delve into a month of hard-going biographies<br /><br />Love/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13916310638803107611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1872825479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1872825479" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1872825479?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1872825479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11613541905707896767"><br/><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This book is (more or less) the written version of Carrie Fisher's stage production "Wishful Drinking." <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264747._SX540_.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Carrie Fisher's stage show 'Wishful Drinking'</b><br/><br/>Carrie is probably best known for her role as the beautiful, intrepid 'Princess Leia" in the Star Wars movies. Carrie was 19 when the first movie filmed and - perhaps coincidentally - this was when the actress transitioned from habitually smoking pot to using hallucinogens and opiates. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264748.jpg' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>Carrie Fisher as Princess Leia</b><br/><br/>In time Carrie became a d</span>
  <span id="freeText11613541905707896767" style="display:none"><br><b>3.5 stars</b><br><br>This book is (more or less) the written version of Carrie Fisher's stage production "Wishful Drinking." <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264747._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher's stage show 'Wishful Drinking'</b><br><br>Carrie is probably best known for her role as the beautiful, intrepid 'Princess Leia" in the Star Wars movies. Carrie was 19 when the first movie filmed and - perhaps coincidentally - this was when the actress transitioned from habitually smoking pot to using hallucinogens and opiates. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264748.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher as Princess Leia</b><br><br>In time Carrie became a drug-addicted alcoholic with manic-depressive disorder (bipolar disorder 2). In this humorous mini-biography - written when Carrie was 52 - the actress relates her story. <br><br>Carrie was born a celebrity, being the child of actress/singer Debbie Reynolds and crooner Eddie Fisher. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264749.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Debbie Reynolds and Eddie Fisher</b><br><br>Debbie starred in iconic films like 'Singin' in the Rain' and Eddie has a long list of oldies, but is 'better known for his scandals than his singing.' In a bombshell incident reminiscent of Brad Pitt leaving Jennifer Aniston for Angelina Jolie, Eddie Fisher left Debbie Reynolds for the gorgeous widow, Elizabeth Taylor. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264750.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Eddie Fisher with Elizabeth Taylor</b><br><br>As it happens Eddie also largely abandoned Carrie and her younger brother Todd. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264752.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Debbie Reynolds and Eddie Fisher with their children Carrie and Todd</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264755._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher with her brother Todd</b><br><br>According to Carrie, Debbie raised the kids in Los Angeles and Eddie 'checked in from time to time' while flitting from one woman to another. Eventually, Eddie married a Chinese woman - Betty Lin - and after she died 'he started to date all of Chinatown.' Carrie notes that 'this was fitting because Eddie had gotten so many facelifts that he looked Asian himself.' LOL<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264758.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Eddie Fisher with Betty Lin</b><br><br>Carrie sang in her mother's nightclub act from the ages of 13 to 17 and - as it happens - also started doing drugs at 13. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264763.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher sang in her mother's nightclub act</b><br><br>Carrie got hold of a bag of pot and 'experimented her brains out' with a friend. Carrie started seeing shrinks at the age of 15.....but was not diagnosed as manic-depressive until years later. By that time Carrie was in her mid-20s, and heavily into alcohol and drugs. She used these 'to turn down the sound [in her head] and smooth her sharp corners.' <br><br>Carrie's second shrink diagnosed her with bipolar disorder 1 and gave her prescription medication - but Carrie didn't want to take it. Instead, the actress jumped on a plane, went to New York and married her boyfriend, singer/songwriter Paul Simon. Carrie notes that her first marriage mirrored her mother's first union - both Paul Simon and Eddie Fisher were 'short, Jewish singers.' <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264761.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264757.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher married her boyfriend Paul Simon</b><br><br>Carrie was in her late 20s when she overdosed and had her stomach pumped. Realizing that her life had become unmanageable, Carrie started attending 12-step programs....thinking alcohol was her big problem. Over the years Carrie had four relapses or 'explosions.' During these she would become sexually promiscuous, spend excessively, and abuse substances. <br><br>Finally, Carrie's third and best psychiatrist correctly diagnosed her with bipolar disorder 2, and medicated her. Unfortunately, two of the pharmaceuticals interacted badly and Carrie was taken off her meds. She ended up psychotic. This eventually led to eletroconvulsive therapy which helped Carrie get better - but robbed her of many memories. Luckily, Carrie had enough remembrances left to write this book.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264760.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher was diagnosed with bipolar disorder</b><br><br>Carrie notes: 'After all the rehabs and all the mental hospitals, I thought to myself, if what doesn't kill you makes you stronger I should be able to lift Cedars Sinai Hospital and glow in the dark.' <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264751.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher learned to live with her mental illness</b><br><br>Interspersed with the tale of Carrie's addiction and mental illness are interesting snippets about her life. Here are a few examples: <br><br>Carrie's stepfather Harry Karl (Debbie's second husband) was not a handsome man, but was wealthy and well-groomed, said to be distinguished looking. Carrie notes, 'That's ugly with money.' To Carrie's amusement, the very handsome Alec Baldwin played Harry in a movie. LOL<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264754.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher's stepfather Harry Karl</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264756.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Alec Baldwin played Harry Karl in the movie 'The Marrying Man'</b><br><br>Harry had a 'barber' (pimp) who showed up every day with a 'manicurist' (wink wink). When Debbie caught on to Harry's shenanigans she high-tailed it to New York with the children - to do a musical. The couple soon divorced.....but not before Harry squandered all of Debbie's money. <br><br>When Todd (Carrie's brother) accidently shot himself in the leg with a gun, Debbie called Carrie from the hospital with the following instructions: 'Rush home and hide all the guns and bullets and flush Todd's marijuana down the toilet. Carrie notes, 'More like a mafia family than a show business one.' <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264762.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Todd Fisher accidentally shot himself</b> <br><br>Carrie adored her mother. She describes Debbie as 'the prettiest, funniest, kindest mother; quick and witty; a consummate performer; and an insanely strong life force.....but a little bit eccentric.' Debbie thought Carrie should have a baby with her (Debbie's) third husband, Richard Hamlett, because he had 'nice eyes.' Carrie declined. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264753.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Debbie Reynolds was a kind, pretty mother </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570568670i/28264810.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Debbie Reynolds with her third husband Richard Hamlett</b><br><br>Carrie had a beautiful daughter, Billie, with her second husband Brian Lourd. When Billie was one, Brian left Carrie for a man named Scott. This devastated the actress.....and perhaps exacerbated her mental illness.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264765._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher with her second husband Brian Lourd</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264759._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Carrie Fisher with her daughter Billie</b> <br><br>After Star Wars became a megahit, Carrie was 'merchandised' into a little doll, a shampoo bottle, a soap, a watch, a Mrs. Potato Head, a Lego figure, a stamp, and a Pez dispenser. Much to Carrie's dismay, she's even a sex doll. Carrie notes, 'If someone tells me to go fuck myself, I can give it a whirl.' Ha ha ha.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264764._SY540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Princess Leia doll</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264767.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Princess Leia Mrs. Potato Head</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264768.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Princess Leia Pez dispenser</b><br><br>Towards the end of the book Carrie acknowledges, 'The place I've arrived at in my life isn't everyone's idea of heavenly....but I'm in a good place.' <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1570567842i/28264766.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Both Carrie Fisher and Debbie Reynolds died in December, 2016 and they're missed. Fortunately, we'll always have their stories and films.<br><br>The book is entertaining and amusing - and provides an instructive and uplifting story about coping with addiction and mental illness. If you're interested in the subject, it's well worth reading. <br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">https://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot....</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11613541905707896767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364626046?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Koivu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Koivu" href="/user/show/1742824-jason-koivu">Jason Koivu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1742824-jason-koivu?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364626046" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10855222760423823810">Like most boys popping wood for the first time in the late '70s and early '80s, I had a "healthy" interest in <s>Princess Leia</s> Carrie Fisher. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392839256i/8620136.jpg' width='400' height='320' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Later in life, whenever I've seen one of her books on the shelves, I'd think about possibly reading it, out of interest for what she might have to say regarding those iconic Star Wars movies. I even gave a little shit about what she's been up to since then. Call it a passing fancy, one that I've passed up time and again for year upon year, right up until rece</span>
  <span id="freeText10855222760423823810" style="display:none">Like most boys popping wood for the first time in the late '70s and early '80s, I had a "healthy" interest in <s>Princess Leia</s> Carrie Fisher. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392839256i/8620136.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Later in life, whenever I've seen one of her books on the shelves, I'd think about possibly reading it, out of interest for what she might have to say regarding those iconic Star Wars movies. I even gave a little shit about what she's been up to since then. Call it a passing fancy, one that I've passed up time and again for year upon year, right up until recently when I found the audiobook version of <i>Wishful Drinking</i> at the library. It was free, I had it in hand and yet still I hesitated and would not have bothered with it except that it is quite short. I wish I'd put it back on the shelf.<br><br>Three hours of listening to anyone famous and privileged talking about their problems is three hours too long. Add to that Fisher's tendency to shout, as if saying it louder makes it funnier. I blame "Laugh In"-era Goldie Hawn for this.<br><br>Negatives aside, Fisher's humor is one of the book's saving graces. She's gone beyond the "woe is me" stage, attained the "let's get our skeletons out of the closet" stage, and she handles it with laughter. <br><br>However, it's a sense of humor that is as dark as the undertones and somewhat depressing subject matter of the entire book. From start to finish, nearly everything within <i>Wishful Drinking</i> is about her struggles with depression, mental illness and substance abuse. It's a hard-knock life. Fisher's taken her knocks and here they are all laid out for you to read. I'm not sure I would recommend it. <br><br><u>Rating</u>: <b>2.5</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10855222760423823810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsten" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsten" href="/user/show/821868-kirsten">Kirsten</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=from-library">from-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/821868-kirsten?shelf=mental-health">mental-health</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53026039" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16248160841233557763">The sad thing about this book is that my favorite part was the cover. I mean, that's a brilliant cover!<br/><br/>But overall? Not the book I was hoping for. Fisher seems to have mostly transcribed her one-woman show, and the problem is, what works for a performance doesn't hold up very well as a book. Everything's sort of glossed over with self-deprecating jokes, and there's not a real sense of narrative or much in the way of self-reflection. I didn't really want a celebrity tell-all, but I would really b</span>
  <span id="freeText16248160841233557763" style="display:none">The sad thing about this book is that my favorite part was the cover. I mean, that's a brilliant cover!<br /><br />But overall? Not the book I was hoping for. Fisher seems to have mostly transcribed her one-woman show, and the problem is, what works for a performance doesn't hold up very well as a book. Everything's sort of glossed over with self-deprecating jokes, and there's not a real sense of narrative or much in the way of self-reflection. I didn't really want a celebrity tell-all, but I would really be interested in what Fisher really thinks and feels about her struggles with addiction, mental illness, and the bizarreness of her fame. Instead, I mostly got a lot of jokes about how it's weird when guys talk about jacking off to Princess Leia. It seemed like whenever she got too close to something painful, it was danced around or told in such a way that felt like she was saying, "Ok, told you about that, got it out of the way, so there." There is some genuinely interesting and affecting material here, but it's hard to find, which is really disappointing.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16248160841233557763" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1625496645?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1625496645" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12451761912270015274"><b>WISHFUL DRINKING</b> is a short, but interesting memoir surrounding Carrie Fisher's life growing up in a celebrity household, <i>(parents Debbie Reynolds and Eddie Fisher)</i> her addictions, electroshock therapy, bipolar disorder and after effects of playing Princess Leia in the epic STAR WARS saga.<p>Written with sarcastic humor and wit, gotta give her credit for laying it all out there, and persevering to overcome her demons.</p><p>Just ok for me.</p></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_147099957" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147099957" />
    <a title="Ellie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2908629-ellie"><img alt="Ellie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399799985p2/2908629.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147099957?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellie" href="/user/show/2908629-ellie">Ellie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2908629-ellie?shelf=film-actors-celebs">film-actors-celebs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2908629-ellie?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147099957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8420892454971833703">I loved Carrie Fisher; she was an icon of my youth. She was also smart, funny, and courageous.<br/><br/>Her death saddened me so much. She should have had years ahead of her. She (and we) were deprived of her wit and intelligence. Her witness to surviving mental illness and addiction.<br/><br/>I read this book in honor of her and to feel her presence again. The book is as funny, poignant, and funny as you would expect. It read like lightening and was over too soon.<br/><br/>Just like Carrie Fisher's life.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2417654112" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2103682022577044679"><i>Wishful Drinking</i> seems like it should be a story that wallows in sadness, but luckily it has a good balance of honesty and humor and breaks through the glamor of the acting world to share the story of a young single mother (who might be better recognized as Princess Leia from the <i>Star Wars</i> franchise) coping with alcoholism and mental illness in a world where such things are generally frowned upon. This is the kind of memoir that really sticks with you after you've read it, it isn't too self-indu</span>
  <span id="freeText2103682022577044679" style="display:none"><i>Wishful Drinking</i> seems like it should be a story that wallows in sadness, but luckily it has a good balance of honesty and humor and breaks through the glamor of the acting world to share the story of a young single mother (who might be better recognized as Princess Leia from the <i>Star Wars</i> franchise) coping with alcoholism and mental illness in a world where such things are generally frowned upon. This is the kind of memoir that really sticks with you after you've read it, it isn't too self-indulgent and it's a courageous story about the dysfunction behind Hollywood magic.</span>

Well, now you can have that experience in book form, written by someone who isn't even your friend.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2285996518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2285996518" />
    <a title="Annie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38036772-annie"><img alt="Annie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586205974p2/38036772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2285996518?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/38036772-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2285996518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer914644188770359119">You know those celebrity memoirs that are clearly ghostwritten, stilted, and pseudo-deep? <br/><br/>Yeah, this isn’t one of those. This is pure Carrie Fisher, demented and crooked and wise and bluntly funny and irreverent.<br/><br/>I really recommend listening to the audiobook. Carrie reads it herself and I think her delivery adds a lot. Plus, of course, it’s rather moving to hear her voice now, as if from the grave. The writing also sounds like something meant to be read aloud, very conversational.<br/><br/>She starts off w</span>
  <span id="freeText914644188770359119" style="display:none">You know those celebrity memoirs that are clearly ghostwritten, stilted, and pseudo-deep? <br /><br />Yeah, this isn’t one of those. This is pure Carrie Fisher, demented and crooked and wise and bluntly funny and irreverent.<br /><br />I really recommend listening to the audiobook. Carrie reads it herself and I think her delivery adds a lot. Plus, of course, it’s rather moving to hear her voice now, as if from the grave. The writing also sounds like something meant to be read aloud, very conversational.<br /><br />She starts off with her incredibly wild childhood as the daughter of Debbie Reynolds and Eddie Fisher. One memorable incident involved her teenage brother accidentally shooting himself in the leg, barely missing his penis, and getting his famous mother Debbie Reynolds arrested and booked for possession of an unlicensed firearm. Debbie then asked her daughter Carrie and her hairdresser Pinkie to go to their house and hide all the firearms and drugs before the police got there, all said in a Transatlantic accent peppered with lots of “dears.” <br /><br />Carrie called her father Puff Daddy because he smoked 4 joints a day, and her mother bought both Carrie and her own mother (i.e. Carrie’s grandmother) vibrators for Christmas. If that doesn’t sum up her childhood, I don’t know what does.<br /><br />Then she proceeds to go through her life as an adult, her fame (someone told her to go fuck herself, so she bought the Princess Leia sex doll and spent hours trying to fuck herself in a hotel room), her struggles with mental illness, and particularly her drug and alcohol dependence. Though it’s heavy material, the book itself is never heavy; Carrie intersperses it all with great humor.<br /><br /><b>Some memorable quotes I bookmarked:</b><br /><br />“My mother thought it would be a good idea for me to have a child with her last husband Richard, because it would have nice eyes. My mother had gone through the change, so she could no longer have children, and Richard had no children of his own yet. And he had nice eyes. My womb was free, and we’re related. Now, my mother didn’t bring this up just once or twice like a normal mother would. She brought it up many many times, mostly while I was driving. And when I finally suggested to her that this might be an odd idea, she said, ‘Oh darling, have you read <i>The Inquirer</i> lately? We live in a very strange world.’ But when <i>The Inquirer</i> becomes your standard for living, you’re in a lot of trouble.”<br /><br />“[That I just had to go to the AA meetings, but didn’t have to like them] was a revelation. I thought I had to like everything I did. And for me, that usually meant I had to take a boatload of dope. Which I did, for many many years. But if what this person told me were true, then I didn’t actually have to be comfortable all the time— if I could in fact learn to experience of quota of discomfort— it would be awesome news.”<br /><br />“I basically just have too much personality for one person, and not quite enough for two.”<br /><br />“Everything seems so much better when you’re infatuated with someone else, and you’re telling each other everything about yourself, like <i>I’m a Libra, I like fireflies on a summer night, I like long moonlit walks on the beach on acid . . . </i>”<br /><br />“You have to sign yourself into the mental hospital. Like commitment papers, I guess. But I was so far gone at the time I didn’t know what I was signing, or doing, so when they finally put the papers in front of me, I took the papers and signed with my left hand, ‘Shame.’ <i>That’s</i> how I signed in for the mental hospital. How sad is that?”<br /><br /><b>~~~~~~~Book Riot's Read Harder Challenge~~~~~~~<br /><br />#12: A celebrity memoir</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="914644188770359119" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41492696" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41492696" />
    <a title="Collin Kelley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1537347-collin-kelley"><img alt="Collin Kelley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541517880p2/1537347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41492696?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Collin Kelley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Collin Kelley" href="/user/show/1537347-collin-kelley">Collin Kelley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41492696" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17798888150113826123">A memoir about drug abuse, sexual compulsion and manic depression shouldn't be this funny, but in Carrie Fisher's hands it's a laugh riot. Wishful Drinking ($21, Simon & Schuster) is slim, packed with photos and basically the script for her hit one-woman show of the same name. Fisher calls this book a "a really, really detailed personals ad," and covers everything from the dead, gay Republican in her bed (which was tabloid fodder for weeks in 2005), her missing-in-action, over-the-top parents (D</span>
  <span id="freeText17798888150113826123" style="display:none">A memoir about drug abuse, sexual compulsion and manic depression shouldn't be this funny, but in Carrie Fisher's hands it's a laugh riot. Wishful Drinking ($21, Simon &amp; Schuster) is slim, packed with photos and basically the script for her hit one-woman show of the same name. Fisher calls this book a "a really, really detailed personals ad," and covers everything from the dead, gay Republican in her bed (which was tabloid fodder for weeks in 2005), her missing-in-action, over-the-top parents (Debbie Reynolds and Eddie Fisher) and, of course, plenty of anecdotes about playing Princess Leia in the original Star Wars trilogy. I plowed through it in one evening, laughing out loud.<br /><br />Fisher has a knack for making the heartbreaking hilarious and there's probably more truth packed into these 176 pages than found in other "memoirs" twice this size (Jane Fonda's bloated tome comes to mind). She talks honestly about her marriage to Paul Simon, her second husband who left her for a man, her father's womanizing (most notoriously leaving Debbie Reynolds for Elizabeth Taylor after her third husband, Mike Todd, was killed in a plane crash), and her electroconvulsive therapy, which she says has done her more good than a dozen shrinks and their pills. Her recollections of Debbie are endearing and juicy, including her gift of a vibrator to 15-year-old Carrie and having Cary Grant call her daughter not once, but twice to talk about the dangers of dropping acid. <br /><br />Perhaps the most hilarious chapter in the book is Carrie's diagram of her whacked out family tree (complete with photos and linking arrows) as she tries to figure out if her teenage daughter is committing incest by dating Elizabeth Taylor's grandson. I actually wish I'd bought the audio book version, because hearing Carrie read this aloud must be a scream.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17798888150113826123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78834799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78834799" />
    <a title="Lena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/220791-lena"><img alt="Lena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589815535p2/220791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78834799?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lena" href="/user/show/220791-lena">Lena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781439153710" href="/book/show/6734757-wishful-drinking">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/220791-lena?shelf=memoir">memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/220791-lena?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78834799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14230774185688174646">It is not often one gets the chance to read the memoirs of someone who has has the dubious distinction of having been made into a Pez dispenser. In Wishful Drinking, Star Wars icon Carrie Fisher has plenty of stories to tell about that and many other fascinating subjects including being raised by famous, scandal-plagued parents, her drug abuse and mental disorder, marriage to Paul Simon, her recent electroconvulsive therapy, and what it's like when a gay republican dies in your bed.<br/><br/>Carrie Fisher</span>
  <span id="freeText14230774185688174646" style="display:none">It is not often one gets the chance to read the memoirs of someone who has has the dubious distinction of having been made into a Pez dispenser. In Wishful Drinking, Star Wars icon Carrie Fisher has plenty of stories to tell about that and many other fascinating subjects including being raised by famous, scandal-plagued parents, her drug abuse and mental disorder, marriage to Paul Simon, her recent electroconvulsive therapy, and what it's like when a gay republican dies in your bed.<br /><br />Carrie Fisher is a very, very funny person, and I frequently laughed out loud while reading this book. Her life is jam-packed with outrageous moments - who else can claim their mother called Cary Grant to counsel them about LSD? As with much good comedy, Fisher's is born of excruciating pain, in her case made all the more extreme by her bi-polar disorder. But she appears to have come out the other side of her illness and suffering, and we can safely enjoy her stories - and the genuine bits of wisdom within them - because of it. <br /><br />My primary complaint about this book is that it was too short. Because it is based on her one-woman show of the same title, it doesn't follow the general conventions of memoir, giving only quick treatment to most of the topics she discusses. You know she has a lot more material when being in rehab with Ozzy Osborne only merits half a line, and her Star Wars experiences could likely have filled a whole book instead of just a short chapter. Because it's also written with the rhythm of a performance, I suspect I might have preferred the audiobook on this one so that I could catch the full nuance of her skilled delivery. But if you've ever felt a burning desire to know why it's a bad idea to wear a bra in space, you'll definitely want to check this out. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14230774185688174646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7776600703396959178" style="display:none">This is a short audiobook that my husband and I listened to in the course of one morning - it is basically a studio recording of a one-woman show that Carrie Fisher did for a while. It is about her life, looking back after electro-shock therapy had discarded some of her memories (terrifying to realize they are still using this treatment!!). She is so funny in how she talks about her father's dalliances and her mother's lifestyle. I do wish the audio engineer had her re-record a few of the parts where she is shouting, but I get it, she has a loud voice. I didn't know all that much about Carrie Fisher but enjoyed this just the same, perhaps more with all the surprises I experienced in not knowing! <br /><br />(If you have Hoopla, it's available there.)</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1694004-joy?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1694004-joy?shelf=celeb-books">celeb-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer11052292937535405254">This is a helluva good memoir! I finished it in one day. Longer review to come ASAP.<br/><br/>Some more thoughts on Wishful Drinking.<br/><br/>I've read several of Carrie Fisher's novels (I recommend Postcards from the Edge) but her memoir is much more fun. It's written in her droll, self-deprecating style and covers her life growing up the daughter of famous parents; the Princess Leia years; her marriages and finally being diagnosed with bipolar disorder. "My diagnosis was manic depression. I think today they call</span>
  <span id="freeText11052292937535405254" style="display:none">This is a helluva good memoir! I finished it in one day. Longer review to come ASAP.<br /><br />Some more thoughts on Wishful Drinking.<br /><br />I've read several of Carrie Fisher's novels (I recommend Postcards from the Edge) but her memoir is much more fun. It's written in her droll, self-deprecating style and covers her life growing up the daughter of famous parents; the Princess Leia years; her marriages and finally being diagnosed with bipolar disorder. "My diagnosis was manic depression. I think today they call it bipolar disorder - so you might say I swing both ways."<br /><br />At the end of the book, Carrie makes a plea for more tolerance regarding mental illness. She writes that she is baffled that there is still is so much stigma regarding mental illness. "At times, being bipolar can be an all-consuming challenge, requiring a lot of stamina and even more courage, so if you're living with this illness and functioning at all, it's something to be proud of, not ashamed of."<br /><br />This is a quick read and I finished the book wishing I could be her friend. She is very funny. Well, as Carrie says, you get the gist of my drift!<br /><br />Now that Carrie has passed away, I'm glad once more that I read this book and encourage everyone to read it too. Very sad that she died so young (she was 60) and her mom, Debbie Reynolds, died of a broken heart a few days later. May they both Rest In Peace. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11052292937535405254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7722467925596305039">I love Carrie's stories. They are funny and interesting. She has a way of bringing out poignant moments amid some absurd situation. She did a lot of living. There is something interesting about seeing what life is like for people who grow up with famous parents. From the outside it looks amazing and she gives a more rounded picture. There are some scenes that overlap with the princess diaries and I wonder if that was on purpose or if that was simply the electro shock therapy. The few repeated st</span>
  <span id="freeText7722467925596305039" style="display:none">I love Carrie's stories. They are funny and interesting. She has a way of bringing out poignant moments amid some absurd situation. She did a lot of living. There is something interesting about seeing what life is like for people who grow up with famous parents. From the outside it looks amazing and she gives a more rounded picture. There are some scenes that overlap with the princess diaries and I wonder if that was on purpose or if that was simply the electro shock therapy. The few repeated stories always come with a new twist and insight. She seems to own her choices and she finds the funny in them. Celebrity opens doors for you in life; I didn't know she married Paul Simon - where have I been. Thanks for sharing Carrie!</span>

<div id="review_146952481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146952481" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146952481?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3124054-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146952481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17328999959899062268">Wishful Drinking is the saddest biography I've ever read. I'm sure die-hard fans of Carrie Fisher may enjoy and appreciate this book, but if you're looking for some fun celebrity comic-relief, definitely pass this one up.<br/><br/>Wishful Drinking begins with Carrie Fisher explaining how proud she is to be starting her life over at the age of fifty-two after having undergone electroshock therapy. She states how she can't remember much of her life up until the writing of Wishful Drinking, and also tries to</span>
  <span id="freeText17328999959899062268" style="display:none">Wishful Drinking is the saddest biography I've ever read. I'm sure die-hard fans of Carrie Fisher may enjoy and appreciate this book, but if you're looking for some fun celebrity comic-relief, definitely pass this one up.<br /><br />Wishful Drinking begins with Carrie Fisher explaining how proud she is to be starting her life over at the age of fifty-two after having undergone electroshock therapy. She states how she can't remember much of her life up until the writing of Wishful Drinking, and also tries to spin bipolar disorder into something normal, light and humorous.<br /><br />Carrie Fisher sprinkles random anecdotes about her life throughout Wishful Drinking, all of which aren't funny at all. I understand she is trying to maintain a positive outlook on her alcoholic, drug-ridden life, but her writing isn't humbling at all; just boastful. If Fisher had reflected more on what she's learned and how she's overcome her problems, then Wishful Drinking might have been more redeeming. Instead, her biography comes across as pathetic. <br /><br />In Hollywood there are many existing celebrities whose parents are celebrities as well, but despite being born into a whirlwind of stardom, the stronger personalities do eventually grow up at some point. <br /><br />When I originally saw Wishful Drinking in the bookstore, I thought to myself, "Wow! Princess Leia is finally going to come forward and share with the world how she overcame her drug and alcohol problems because she's finally grown up and learned something!" Boy was I wrong! <br /><br />I recommend Wishful Drinking only to the faithful fans of Carrie Fisher.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17328999959899062268" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2370776563575689902">A friend let me know about this wonderful audiobook,and I'm so glad she did. I loved it! Loved listening to Carrie's voice for three hours straight. She was so narural as a narrator. And despite talking about very diffucult things,did it with humor. I found myself laughing out loud many times. <br/><br/>Being a Star Wars fan,of course my favourite parts were when she talked about that. At the end of the book she reads the,now classic,line of her asking help from Obi Wan. And then goes "I can't forget that</span>
  <span id="freeText2370776563575689902" style="display:none">A friend let me know about this wonderful audiobook,and I'm so glad she did. I loved it! Loved listening to Carrie's voice for three hours straight. She was so narural as a narrator. And despite talking about very diffucult things,did it with humor. I found myself laughing out loud many times. <br /><br />Being a Star Wars fan,of course my favourite parts were when she talked about that. At the end of the book she reads the,now classic,line of her asking help from Obi Wan. And then goes "I can't forget that stupid fucking hologram speech! That's why I did dope!" It made me lol at the supermarket check out. That was Carrie. She talked about her drug use and mental illness,hard stuff. But she had this awesome sense of humor. <br /><br /><br />I'm happy I listened to this. It made me feel a little bit closer to her,getting to know her more. For me,she'll always be princess Leia,and then later general Organa,and that's okay. I know there were so much more to her,but her role as Leia meant the world to me and had a huge impact on me. <br />I'm grateful for this short audiobook for making me think about her again,and giving me a reason to write about her. And about Leia. <br />Fisher did great job with talking about mental illness,ending the silence surrounding it. She will be greatly missed. <br />Go listen to this,you won't regret it. </span>

<div id="review_49954388" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49954388" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/895467-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242077700p2/895467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49954388?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/895467-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who wish to learn a bit more about Carrie Fischer and Star Wars and everything in between...</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/895467-kelly?shelf=autobiography">autobiography</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49954388" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1205443514739968361">This has to be one of the funniest biographies I've ever read. Fischer's frankness reminded me of Esther Williams' autobiography <i>The Million Dollar Mermaid</i>. And what she does tell is pretty cut and dry with no euphemisms (for example Fischer describes that when Elizabeth Taylor's husband died in a tragic accident, her father "consoled her with his penis").<br/><br/>It's a very short read and that might be my biggest complaint. "You wouldn't believe what I'm NOT telling you," Fischer teases in her book. An</span>
  <span id="freeText1205443514739968361" style="display:none">This has to be one of the funniest biographies I've ever read. Fischer's frankness reminded me of Esther Williams' autobiography <i>The Million Dollar Mermaid</i>. And what she does tell is pretty cut and dry with no euphemisms (for example Fischer describes that when Elizabeth Taylor's husband died in a tragic accident, her father "consoled her with his penis").<br /><br />It's a very short read and that might be my biggest complaint. "You wouldn't believe what I'm NOT telling you," Fischer teases in her book. And I know that she's leaving out tons because whenever she's on a talk show promoting her book she always has something new to say. For instance, on the set of <i>Star Wars</i>, Mark Hamill was a huge fan of Alec Guinness. And eventually he got so annoyed with Mark Hamill asking him all these questions, Alec gave him 20 pounds to go away. Which Mark actually did...after Alec signed the 20 pounds. <br /><br />When on NPR's <i>Wait Wait...Don't Tell Me!</i>, Peter Sagal asked her when she was going to come out with the full uncut biography. She replied, "When all the people those stories relate to are dead. Including ME!"<br />So I will be left to consider how big the uncut biography of Carrie Fischer is in comparison to Esther Williams' and (god forbid) Bill Clinton's biographies. I only hope that she does eventually write a full biography because that would be a fantastic read. But then again maybe she wants some secrets to stay secret. And for a "Hollywood Inbreed" celebrity whose life was always in the open, she probably deserves that privacy.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1205443514739968361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fafPFaebHf9BqimoLt99k8FXtFMkB4uMaPRwVe+zveetwVST9qK/lH4epr01eTQMc27opKq9NBus2d1Rd3mKWQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8N63QghRnW99urcQyPcmRCBjWBOAVswifE/Pkt0+elEguCzEWWg/BEIOOAXTUW/bkloE5A7sc7W4YmKWRfRN7w==')})
  }

After two broken marriages, this third, she believed, was her lucky charm. But within a few years, Debbie discovered that he had betrayed her emotionally and financially, nearly destroying her life.\n\nToday, she writes, &quot;When I read the optimistic ending of my last memoir now, I can\'t believe how naive I was when I wrote it. In Unsinkable, I look back at the many years since then, and share my memories of a film career that took me from the Miss Burbank Contest of 1948 to the work I did in 2012. . . . To paraphrase Bette Davis: Fasten your seatbelts, I\'ve had a bumpy ride.&quot;\n\nUnsinkable shines a spotlight on the resilient woman whose talent and passion for her work have endured for more than six decades. In her engaging, down-to-earth voice, Debbie shares private details about her man and money troubles, including building and losing her Las Vegas dream hotel and her treasured Hollywood memorabilia collection. Yet no matter how difficult the problems, the show always goes on.\n\nDebbie also invites us into the close circle of her family, speaking with deep affection and honesty about her relationships with her children, Carrie and Todd Fisher. She looks back at her life as an actress during Hollywood\'s Golden Age—&quot;the most magical time you could imagine&quot;—including her lifelong friendship with (and years-long estrangement from) the legendary Elizabeth Taylor. Here, too, are stories that never reached the tabloids about numerous celebrities, such as Ava Gardner, Clark Gable, Frank Sinatra, Mick Jagger, Gene Kelly, and many more. She takes us on a guided tour through her movies with delightful, often hilarious behind-the-scenes anecdotes about every film in which she was involved, from 1948 to the present.\n\nFrank and forthright, and featuring dozens of previously unseen photos from Debbie\'s personal collection, Unsinkable is a poignant reminder that there is light in the darkest times. By 1978 he was the biggest concert draw in the history of stand-up. In 1981 he quit forever. This book is, in his own words, the story of &quot;why I did stand-up and why I walked away.&quot; \n\nEmmy and Grammy Award winner, author of the acclaimed New York Times bestsellers Shopgirl and The Pleasure of My Company, and a regular contributor to The New Yorker, Martin has always been a writer. His memoir of his years in stand-up is candid, spectacularly amusing, and beautifully written. \n\nAt age ten Martin started his career at Disneyland, selling guidebooks in the newly opened theme park. In the decade that followed, he worked in the Disney magic shop and the Bird Cage Theatre at Knott\'s Berry Farm, performing his first magic/comedy act a dozen times a week. The story of these years, during which he practiced and honed his craft, is moving and revelatory. The dedication to excellence and innovation is formed at an astonishingly early age and never wavers or wanes. \n\nMartin illuminates the sacrifice, discipline, and originality that made him an icon and informs his work to this day. To be this good, to perform so frequently, was isolating and lonely. It took Martin decades to reconnect with his parents and sister, and he tells that story with great tenderness. Martin also paints a portrait of his times-the era of free love and protests against the war in Vietnam, the heady irreverence of The Smothers Brothers Comedy Hour in the late sixties, and the transformative new voice of Saturday Night Live in the seventies.\n\nThroughout the text, Martin has placed photographs, many never seen before. Born Standing Up is a superb testament to the sheer tenacity, focus, and daring of one of the greatest and most iconoclastic comedians of all time.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"943739173738095615\" The essay “What It Was Like, Part Two” reveals how it felt to pick up the role again nine years later, and what doing so has meant to her.\n \nSome more things you will learn about Lauren: She once tried to go vegan just to bond with Ellen DeGeneres, she’s aware that meeting guys at awards shows has its pitfalls (“If you’re meeting someone for the first time after three hours of hair, makeup, and styling, you’ve already set the bar too high”), and she’s a card-carrying REI shopper (“My bungee cords now earn points!”).\n \nIncluding photos and excerpts from the diary Graham kept during the <span id="freeTextContainer10843579111049051189">Carrie Fisher was an American actress, screenwriter and author, most famous for her portrayal of Princess Leia in the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy. Fisher was the daughter of singer <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/351430._Eddie_Fisher' title=' Eddie Fisher' rel='nofollow noopener'> Eddie Fisher</a> and actress <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/223415._Debbie_Reynolds' title=' Debbie Reynolds' rel='nofollow noopener'> Debbie Reynolds</a>. She had one daughter, Billie Lourd (b. 1992). <br/><br/>Her final film, <i>Star Wars: The Last Jedi</i>, was released on December 15, 2017 and is dedicated to her.</span>
